</dl>
<p>The medium quality photo uses only 4.3% of the storage space required for the uncompressed image, but has little noticeable loss of detail or visible artifacts. However, once a certain threshold of compression is passed, compressed images show increasingly visible defects. See the article on <a href="/wiki/Rate%E2%80%93distortion_theory" title="Rateâdistortion theory">rateâdistortion theory</a> for a mathematical explanation of this threshold effect. A particular limitation of JPEG in this regard is its non-overlapped 8Ã8 block transform structure. More modern designs such as <a href="/wiki/JPEG_2000" title="JPEG 2000">JPEG 2000</a> and <a href="/wiki/JPEG_XR" title="JPEG XR">JPEG XR</a> exhibit a more graceful degradation of quality as the bit usage decreasesÂ â by using transforms with a larger spatial extent for the lower frequency coefficients and by using overlapping transform basis functions.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lossless_further_compression">Lossless further compression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPEG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Lossless further compression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>From 2004 to 2008 new research emerged on ways to further compress the data contained in JPEG images without modifying the represented image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauermann_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bauermann-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ponomarenko_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ponomarenko-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stirner_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-stirner-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matsuda_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-matsuda-28">[28]</a></sup> This has applications in scenarios where the original image is only available in JPEG format, and its size needs to be reduced for archiving or transmission. Standard general-purpose compression tools cannot significantly compress JPEG files.</p>
<p>Typically, such schemes take advantage of improvements to the naive scheme for coding DCT coefficients, which fails to take into account:</p>
<ul>
<li>Correlations between magnitudes of adjacent coefficients in the same block;</li>
<li>Correlations between magnitudes of the same coefficient in adjacent blocks;</li>
<li>Correlations between magnitudes of the same coefficient/block in different channels;</li>
<li>The DC coefficients when taken together resemble a downscale version of the original image multiplied by a scaling factor. Well-known schemes for <a href="/wiki/Lossless_compression#Graphics" title="Lossless compression">lossless coding of continuous-tone images</a> can be applied, achieving somewhat better compression than the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huffman_code" title="Huffman code">Huffman coded</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DPCM" title="DPCM">DPCM</a> used in JPEG.</li>
</ul>
<p>Some standard but rarely used options already exist in JPEG to improve the efficiency of coding DCT coefficients: the <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic_coding" title="Arithmetic coding">arithmetic coding</a> option, and the progressive coding option (which produces lower bitrates because values for each coefficient are coded independently, and each coefficient has a significantly different distribution). Modern methods have improved on these techniques by reordering coefficients to group coefficients of larger magnitude together;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauermann_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bauermann-25">[25]</a></sup> using adjacent coefficients and blocks to predict new coefficient values;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stirner_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-stirner-27">[27]</a></sup> dividing blocks or coefficients up among a small number of independently coded models based on their statistics and adjacent values;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ponomarenko_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ponomarenko-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stirner_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-stirner-27">[27]</a></sup> and most recently, by decoding blocks, predicting subsequent blocks in the spatial domain, and then encoding these to generate predictions for DCT coefficients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matsuda_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-matsuda-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Typically, such methods can compress existing JPEG files between 15 and 25 percent, and for JPEGs compressed at low-quality settings, can produce improvements of up to 65%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stirner_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-stirner-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matsuda_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-matsuda-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>A freely available tool called packJPG<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> is based on the 2007 paper "Improved Redundancy Reduction for JPEG Files."</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Derived_formats_for_stereoscopic_3D">Derived formats for stereoscopic 3D</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPEG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Derived formats for stereoscopic 3D">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="JPEG_Stereoscopic">JPEG Stereoscopic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPEG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: JPEG Stereoscopic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JPS-sample.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="3720" height="64" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/JPS-sample.jpg/220px-JPS-sample.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/JPS-sample.jpg/330px-JPS-sample.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/JPS-sample.jpg/440px-JPS-sample.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JPS-sample.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An example of a stereoscopic .JPS file</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>JPS is a stereoscopic JPEG image used for creating 3D effects from 2D images. It contains two static images, one for the left eye and one for the right eye; encoded as two side-by-side images in a single JPG file. JPEG Stereoscopic (JPS, extension .jps) is a JPEG-based format for <a href="/wiki/Stereoscopy" title="Stereoscopy">stereoscopic</a> images.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> It has a range of configurations stored in the JPEG APP3 marker field, but usually contains one image of double width, representing two images of identical size in cross-eyed (i.e. left frame on the right half of the image and vice versa) side-by-side arrangement. This file format can be viewed as a JPEG without any special software, or can be processed for rendering in other modes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="JPEG_Multi-Picture_Format">JPEG Multi-Picture Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPEG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: JPEG Multi-Picture Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>JPEG Multi-Picture Format (MPO, extension .mpo) is a JPEG-based format for multi-view images. It contains two or more JPEG files concatenated together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> There are also special EXIF fields describing its purpose. This is used by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fujifilm_FinePix_Real_3D_W1" title="Fujifilm FinePix Real 3D W1">Fujifilm FinePix Real 3D W1</a> camera, <a href="/wiki/Panasonic_Lumix_DMC-TZ20" title="Panasonic Lumix DMC-TZ20">Panasonic Lumix DMC-TZ20</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panasonic_Lumix_DMC-TZ30" title="Panasonic Lumix DMC-TZ30">DMC-TZ30</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Panasonic_Lumix_DMC-TZ60&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Panasonic Lumix DMC-TZ60 (page does not exist)">DMC-TZ60</a>&amp; DMC-TS4 (FT4), <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> DSC-HX7V, <a href="/wiki/HTC_Evo_3D" title="HTC Evo 3D">HTC Evo 3D</a>, the JVC GY-HMZ1U AVCHD/MVC extension camcorder and by the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_3DS" title="Nintendo 3DS">Nintendo 3DS</a> for its 3D Camera. In the last few years, due to the growing use of stereoscopic images, much effort has been spent by the scientific community to develop algorithms for stereoscopic image compression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Patent_issues">Patent issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPEG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Patent issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2002, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forgent_Networks" title="Forgent Networks">Forgent Networks</a> asserted that it owned and would enforce <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patent</a> rights on the JPEG technology, arising from a patent that had been filed on October 27, 1986, and granted on October 6, 1987 (<span><a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/patents/US4698672" rel="nofollow">U.S. Patent 4,698,672</a></span>). The announcement created a furor reminiscent of <a href="/wiki/Unisys" title="Unisys">Unisys</a>' attempts to assert its rights over the GIF image compression standard.</p>
<p>The JPEG committee investigated the patent claims in 2002 and were of the opinion that they were invalidated by <a href="/wiki/Prior_art" title="Prior art">prior art</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Others also concluded that Forgent did not have a patent that covered JPEG.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Nevertheless, between 2002 and 2004 Forgent was able to obtain about US$105 million by licensing their patent to some 30 companies. In April 2004, Forgent sued 31 other companies to enforce further license payments. In July of the same year, a consortium of 21 large computer companies filed a countersuit, with the goal of invalidating the patent. In addition, Microsoft launched a separate lawsuit against Forgent in April 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In February 2006, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a> agreed to re-examine Forgent's JPEG patent at the request of the <a href="/wiki/Public_Patent_Foundation" title="Public Patent Foundation">Public Patent Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reexam_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-reexam-39">[39]</a></sup> On May 26, 2006 the USPTO found the patent invalid based on <a href="/wiki/Prior_art" title="Prior art">prior art</a>. The USPTO also found that Forgent knew about the <a href="/wiki/Prior_art" title="Prior art">prior art</a>, and did not tell the Patent Office, making any appeal to reinstate the patent highly unlikely to succeed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Forgent also possesses a similar patent granted by the European Patent Office in 1994, though it is unclear how enforceable it is.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ep266049_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-ep266049-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of October 27, 2006, the U.S. patent's 20-year term appears to have expired, and in November 2006, Forgent agreed to abandon enforcement of patent claims against use of the JPEG standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-surrendered_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-surrendered-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The JPEG committee has as one of its explicit goals that their standards (in particular their baseline methods) be implementable without payment of license fees, and they have secured appropriate license rights for their <a href="/wiki/JPEG_2000" title="JPEG 2000">JPEG 2000</a> standard from over 20 large organizations.</p>
<p>Beginning in August 2007, another company, Global Patent Holdings, LLC claimed that its patent (<span><a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/patents/US5253341" rel="nofollow">U.S. Patent 5,253,341</a></span>) issued in 1993, is infringed by the downloading of JPEG images on either a website or through e-mail. If not invalidated, this patent could apply to any website that displays JPEG images. The patent emerged<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title='how can it emerge in 2007 when a cite below has "In autumn 2000 ..." (February 2010)'>clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in July 2007 following a seven-year reexamination by the U.S. Patent and Trademark Office in which all of the original claims of the patent were revoked, but an additional claim (claim 17) was confirmed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPHLaw1_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPHLaw1-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In its first two lawsuits following the reexamination, both filed in Chicago, Illinois, Global Patent Holdings sued the Green Bay Packers, CDW, Motorola, Apple, Orbitz, Officemax, Caterpillar, Kraft and Peapod as defendants. A third lawsuit was filed on December 5, 2007 in South Florida against ADT Security Services, AutoNation, Florida Crystals Corp., HearUSA, MovieTickets.com, Ocwen Financial Corp. and Tire Kingdom, and a fourth lawsuit on January 8, 2008 in South Florida against the Boca Raton Resort &amp; Club. A fifth lawsuit was filed against Global Patent Holdings in Nevada. That lawsuit was filed by Zappos.com, Inc., which was allegedly threatened by Global Patent Holdings, and seeks a judicial declaration that the '341 patent is invalid and not infringed.</p>
<p>Global Patent Holdings had also used the '341 patent to sue or threaten outspoken critics of broad software patents, including Gregory Aharonian<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPHLaw2_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPHLaw2-44">[44]</a></sup> and the anonymous operator of a website blog known as the "Patent Troll Tracker."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPHLaw3_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPHLaw3-45">[45]</a></sup> On December 21, 2007, patent lawyer Vernon Francissen of Chicago asked the U.S. Patent and Trademark Office to reexamine the sole remaining claim of the '341 patent on the basis of new prior art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPHLaw4_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPHLaw4-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 5, 2008, the U.S. Patent and Trademark Office agreed to reexamine the '341 patent, finding that the new prior art raised substantial new questions regarding the patent's validity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPHLaw11_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPHLaw11-47">[47]</a></sup> In light of the reexamination, the accused infringers in four of the five pending lawsuits have filed motions to suspend (stay) their cases until completion of the U.S. Patent and Trademark Office's review of the '341 patent. On April 23, 2008, a judge presiding over the two lawsuits in Chicago, Illinois granted the motions in those cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPHLaw55_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPHLaw55-48">[48]</a></sup> On July 22, 2008, the Patent Office issued the first "Office Action" of the second reexamination, finding the claim invalid based on nineteen separate grounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPHLaw66_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPHLaw66-49">[49]</a></sup> On Nov. 24, 2009, a Reexamination Certificate was issued cancelling all claims.</p>
<p>Beginning in 2011 and continuing as of early 2013, an entity known as Princeton Digital Image Corporation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PDICTroll_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-PDICTroll-50">[50]</a></sup> based in Eastern Texas, began suing large numbers of companies for alleged infringement of <span><a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/patents/US4813056" rel="nofollow">U.S. Patent 4,813,056</a></span>. Princeton claims that the JPEG image compression standard infringes the '056 patent and has sued large numbers of websites, retailers, camera and device manufacturers and resellers. The patent was originally owned and assigned to General Electric. The patent expired in December 2007, but Princeton has sued large numbers of companies for "past infringement" of this patent. (Under U.S. patent laws, a patent owner can sue for "past infringement" up to six years before the filing of a lawsuit, so Princeton could theoretically have continued suing companies until December 2013.) As of March 2013, Princeton had suits pending in New York and Delaware against more than 55 companies. General Electric's involvement in the suit is unknown, although court records indicate that it assigned the patent to Princeton in 2009 and retains certain rights in the patent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PDICTroll2_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-PDICTroll2-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Implementations">Implementations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPEG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Implementations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A very important implementation of a JPEG codec is the free programming library <i><a href="/wiki/Libjpeg" title="Libjpeg">libjpeg</a></i> of the Independent JPEG Group. It was first published in 1991 and was key for the success of the standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPEG-homepage_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-JPEG-homepage-52">[52]</a></sup> This library or a direct derivative of it is used in countless applications.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPEG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
